How to design a baseball database

Published: Mon 03 June 2019
By Suhasini Radhakrishnan

In Posts.

tags: python Sqlite3 DbDesigner

Baseball database design¶

In this project we will be working with the base basll Major League Data found in Retrosheet. https://www.retrosheet.org/

The main file that we will be working with combines 127 seperate csv files from retrosheet and is in game_log.csv.We will normalise the datapoints in this table to create a database structure.

In addition to the main files, there are helper files also sourced from Retrosheet:

  • park_codes.csv
  • person_codes.csv
  • team_codes.csv

The data dictionaru for the events can be found here - http://www.retrosheet.org/eventfile.htm

import pandas as pd import matplotlib.pyplot as plt import matplotlib.style as style import sqlite3 import numpy as np

setting to avoid data trucation¶

pd.set_option('max_columns', 180) pd.set_option('max_rows', 200000) pd.set_option('max_colwidth', 5000)

the person_id in the person_code reference data corresponds to the 'XX_id' in the game_logs. They are the ids associated with the manager, player coach and umpire names. The teamids are associated wiht h_name and v_name in the game log. The team table provides more information about a team, the league and the corresponding franchise Id.

for the game_log We have data from 1871 - 2016.

game_log seem to have information about

  • general information on the game
  • the information on the winning teaam and losing team
  • player's position and the names along with umpiers for the position
  • statistics on hosting and visiting team

Let us have a look at the teamnames and leagues

def league_info(league):
    league_games = game_log[game_log['h_league'] ==league]
    earliest = league_games['date'].min()
    latest = league_games['date'].max()
    print("{} played games from {} to {}".format(league,earliest, latest))
    
    
for league in game_log['h_league'].unique():
    league_info(league)

There are cases when the team assumes a different name, in different city and league, but is represented by the same franchise id

There are multiple defensive position numbers in data set. Let us find out what do they mean - According to https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baseball_positions we have the following positions - * 1 (pitcher) * 2 (catcher) * 3 (first baseman) * 4 (second baseman)* * 5 (third baseman) * 6 (shortstop) * 7 (left fielder) * 8 (center fielder) * 9 (right fielders) To insert the data in the database, we need a primary key for each column. Retosheet talks about the unique ids in here - https://www.retrosheet.org/eventfile.htm They define Ids as - Each game begins with a twelve character ID record which identifies the date, home team, and number of the game. For example, ATL198304080 should be read as follows. The first three characters identify the home team (the Braves). The next four are the year (1983). The next two are the month (April) using the standard numeric notation, 04, followed by the day (08). The last digit indicates if this is a single game (0), first game (1) or second game (2) if more than one game is played during a day, usually a double header The id record starts the description of a game thus ending the description of the preceding game in the file. We will try to create this Id while storing the table in DB.

Import data into the database¶

We will go ahead and create the database in the in Sqlite. There are three ways to do this

  • Using python SQLlite library - This gives us the highest level of control over reading and writing the data. But is highly manual
  • Using pandas - This is a handy method, but pandas sometimes converts the datatype while reading in automatically. Also the data needs to be small enough to be accomodated in momory
  • Using SQLite shell - This is a easy method. But we run into some problems ascertaining datatypes based on the first row of the data, need to remove the header while reading the data and so on. However, we may not always have access to the shell.

For this excercise, we will be using pandas method.

In [195]:
# Create functions needed to see this through.

database = "mlb.db"

# function to run a query
def run_query(q):
    with sqlite3.connect(database) as conn:
        return pd.read_sql(q,conn)
    
# function to return not table objects such as views
def run_command(q):
    with sqlite3.connect(database) as conn:
        conn.isolation_level = None
        conn.execute(q)
        
# function show the list of all table and view

def show_tables():
    q = '''
        SELECT 
            name
            , type
        FROM sqlite_master
        WHERE type IN ('table', 'view')
    '''
    return run_query(q)

Ideally we would like to create a source schema to store out tables but as the only schemas allowed in sqllite are main and temp we ill go ahead and use SRC_tablename convention for source table.

In [191]:
#create a dictionary mapping the required SQL table name to the pandas tablename
table_data= {
    'SRC_game_log' : game_log
    , 'SRC_park_codes':park_codes
    , 'SRC_person_codes': person_code
    , 'SRC_team' : team
}

with sqlite3.connect(database) as conn:
    for table_name, data in table_data.items():
        conn.execute("DROP TABLE IF EXISTS {};".format(table_name))
        data.to_sql(table_name,conn, index = False)

Based on the above description of the primary id, we should look at h_name, date, h_game_number field. Let us see of there are any duplicates with this combination

In [193]:
q1 = '''
    SELECT 
    
          h_name||date||h_game_number
          , count(*)
    FROM SRC_game_log
    group by h_name||date||h_game_number
    Having count(*) > 1

'''

run_query(q1)
Out[193]:
h_name||date||h_game_number count(*)

There are no duplicates in this column and therefore can be used safely as a key

Normalise the data¶

  • We see in the gme_log that the all the id fields are followed by the name. This information is present in the person_code table. Therefore we will go ahead and remove the name fields. We should also note that the game_log is all about the game. But the player name provides us information about the player.

  • in the game_log we see the name of the team paired wiht the league name. But we get the same information from the team table. We can drop the league name field for both the visiting and the hosting team from the game log

  • In the park_codes table, we see the start date and the end date signifying the dates when the game was played at the park. This information can be obtained from the 'date' column of the game_log table and hence we will drop this

  • in game_log, we have a listing for 9 players on each team with their positions - we can remove these and have one table that tracks player appearances and their positions.

We will use the following DB table to create our database. we will first create the tables that do not have any foregin key - person , person_apprearance, apprearance_type, and park

Create the Database¶

# Create the table person. Since these are the reference table, we will prefix them with ODS

q5 = '''
    CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS Person(
        person_id NVARCHAR(50) PRIMARY KEY
        ,first_name TEXT
        ,last_name TEXT
);
    
'''

run_command(q5)

    SELECT

        ,last
        , first 
    FROM SRC_person_codes;

    CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS league(
        league_id NVARCHAR(50)
        , league_name TEXT

# inserting the data into the table

leagues = {
'NL': 'National League'
,'AL': 'American League'
,'AA': 'American Association'
,'FL': 'Federal League'
,'PL': 'Players League'
,'UA': 'Union Association'}


with sqlite3.connect(database) as conn:
    for identity,name in leagues.items():
        q = ''' INSERT OR IGNORE INTO league VALUES("{}", "{}")'''.format (identity,name)
        conn.isolation_level = None
        conn.execute(q)
